rates his or her leadership which supported Hammond et al. (1997) argument that rational and 
intuitive style should not be rigidly placed on the ends of a continuum instead an individuals 
relative standing between these two styles should determine his or her style, where an intuitive 
decision maker should share some rationality and a rational decision maker should consider some 
intuition to make superior choices, which support the proposed mixed environment driven model 
to decision making process of this study. This proposed mixed model support the argument of 
Spicer & Sadler- Smith (2005) that a balanced approach in decision making can be more appropriate 
for effective decision making. So, effective decisions can be made, when all decision-making styles 
proposed by the mixed model are taken into consideration by different levels of management in 
organisations. 
So, to summarize on the mixed environment driven model to decision-making processes, the 
more complex, dynamic, and poor environment the more intuition and heuristic, the less rational. On 
the other hand, the more simple, stable, and rich environment the more rational, the less intuition and 
heuristic.  
Findings and results of this case study can be used in Qatar to fill the gaps in practicing 
decision-making styles by government departments and other private sector institutions to enhance 
effectiveness of decision-making processes and help in capacity building programs tackling human 
resources development regarding decision-making domain and other domains of leadership and 
management in institutions across the country. The mixed environment driven model to decision-
making processes, can be used in Qatar and elsewhere to face the challenges that the environment 
present in terms of complexity dynamism and scarcity of resources.  
6.4 CONTRIBUTION TO KNOWLEDGE  
The current research contributes not only to theory, but also to practice. The following two 
subsections highlight the corresponding contributions. 
6.4.1 CONTRIBUTIONS TO THEORY 
The contributions to theory coming from this research are multifold and can be summarized 
as follows: 
1) Providing a comprehensive and critical review of recent and classified literature related to 
decision-making styles. The literature review conducted in this research is comprehensive and 
critical. Thus, it will be useful for researchers and other stakeholders interested in this domain. 
This is because such a review can be used by other researcher to understand what has been 
done in this domain and what has been left behind. This significant in showing the gaps that 
can be fulfilled to improve the related body of knowledge. 
2) Providing a theoretical model that can be used by researchers and presenting a case study 
concerning the integration of rational and heuristic elements in executive decision-making 
process in a developing country. This study is the first in its nature in Qatar and can be used 
for further investigation in this domain. 
6.4.2 CONTRIBUTIONS TO PRACTICE  
1) This thesis is a study of decision-making process it assesses decision-making elements 
(heuristics and rational) across Qatari executive managers and attempts to formulate guidelines 
for improving these elements. Current research in the field has only explored elements of good 
decision quality, and smart organisations in contrast extraordinarily little guidance is available 
for organisations to improve their decision-making abilities. This research identifies decision-
making styles and develop a model that businesses can use to improve their decision-making 
capabilities. 
2) The findings and results of this case study can be used in Qatar to fill the gaps in practicing 
decision-making styles by government departments and other private sector institutions to 
enhance effectiveness of decision-making processes. This will further help in capacity building 
programs tackling human resources development regarding decision-making domain which 
will also reflect positively on other domains of human resources development that can establish 
a high level of leadership and management in institutions across the country. 
3) The mixed environment driven model to decision-making processes, can be used in Qatar and 
elsewhere to face the challenges that the environment present in terms of complexity dynamism 
and richness.  
6.5 RESEARCH LIMITATIONS  
This study has the following limitations: 
1) Difficulties to assess the targeted population of different level of executive decision makers in 
Qatar in both public and private institutions. 
2) Difficulties in developing cluster samples to reflect different specialization in government and 
private institutions. 
3) The most important limitation of this study is that the lack of prior studies dedicated to the 
decision-making style in Qatar. However, this lack of studies was the main reason for 
conducting the study but as yet limits the research's ability to compare with other studies in 
order to confirm the external reliability of the questionnaire. 
4) Limitations related to environmental issues concerning COVID-19 which reflected negatively 
on administering the right process of sampling and hindered the process of conducting and 
analysing qualitative interviews that would lead to theory saturation.  
6.6 AREAS FOR FURTHER RESEARCH  
6.6.1 AREAS CONCERNING THE METHODOLOGY 
In this case study, subjects from one population participated in this research, where the 
research instrument was evaluated using one sample in a hope that this sample will represent the 
whole population. The researcher believe that the population of executive decision makers is 
spread over different discipline and specializations within different types of organisations whether 
organic or mechanistic types of organisations in both public and private sectors or different in the 
aspects of value creation. This should entail that the population of executive decision makers to be 
heterogeneous rather than homogeneous should be considered. If this concept proves to be correct, 
then the researcher recommends the following: 
1) Future researchers in this domain should start initially investigating this issue and go deep in 
analysing the population of executive decision makers in Qatar for clustering purposes and 
developing a database that is helpful in accomplishing research objectives and administering 
different phases of the research. 
2)  Develop and administer cluster samples that provide good representation of internally 
heterogeneous populations. 
3) Administering three cluster samples to be administered in three stages using the same 
theoretical model with the moderating variable. These three samples correspond with the three 
decision making levels that include a) operational decisions, b) managerial decisions and c) 
strategic decisions.  
4) Develop orientation mechanisms for participants that can reflect positively to accomplishing 
research objectives. This can be done by creating a sense of urgency in the minds of leaders on 
the national level to this type of study and ensuring the benefits of being ground in any future 
capacity building programs related to human resources development. 
6.6.2 RECOMMENDATIONS FOR FURTHER RESEARCH 
In addition to the recommendations concerning the methodology and methods made in this 
research and briefly highlighted and discussed in the previous section, this research also provides 
some important avenues for future research to continue developing this important research domain, 
adding to the theoretical model moderating variables, like training programs, empowerment and 
capacity building programs, between independent and dependent variables to check if these 
moderating variables can influence the process of decision making. 
6.7 ACHIEVEMENT OF THE AIM AND OBJECTIVES 
The aim of this research is to analyse in detail the decision-making processes and the use 
of rational and heuristics elements in executives decision-making processes in Qatar, this was 
shown to be so, and has been detailed in chapters 4 and 5 of the thesis, and he research answers 
several specific questions, related to different decision-making styes which have not yet been 
answered by the available extant literature in general and specifically in the Qatari context. 
The objectives of this study are as follows and are connected to the research questions: 
O1: To investigate the managers awareness and understanding of the applied mix of 
decision-making styles, including rational and heuristic styles, in executive decision-making in 
Qatar (RQ1 and RQ2),  
O2: To investigate the relationship of decision-making styles with executives strategic 
contexts (RQ2 and RQ3),  
O3: To investigate the relationship of decision-making styles with executives 
demographics (RQ2 and RQ3), 
O4: To suggest the direction of improvement, derived from relevant academic research, by 
which executives' decision-making should follow (RQ5). 
Results of the study show that respondents exhibited all six decision-making styles with 
different level of agreement Figure 5.1 (Objective 1). The results developed from the descriptive 
analysis of the average percentage to respondents responses (Agree and Strongly agree) of scale 
items of each factor taking separately, where 88.2% agree and strongly agree on rational decision-
making style, 50.85% agree and strongly agree on intuitive decision-making style, 64.5% agree 
and strongly agree on dependent decision-making style, 20.76% agree and strongly agree on 
avoidant decision-making style, 95.8% agreement on expert heuristic decision-making style and 
22.85% agreement on spontaneous decision-making style. What does that mean? From the total 
respondents 27.9% agree and strongly agree on expert heuristic decision-making style, 25.72% 
agree and strongly agree on rational decision-making style, 14.82% agree and strongly agree on 
intuitive decision-making style, 18.8% agree and strongly agree on dependent decision-making 
style, 6.66% agree and strongly agree on spontaneous decision-making style, and 6.1% agree and 
strongly agree on avoidant decision-making style.  
These findings confirm the argument that decision making is a multifaceted and multi-
dimensional phenomenon, where the focus in decision making varies from in different contexts 
and from discipline to discipline. Table 4.15 shows how the six decision-making factors differ 
significantly with different strategic contexts (Objective 2) and H01 (that here is NO Statistically 
Significant (<0.05) difference between decision-making styles of executives and their strategic 
contexts in Qatar) is only partially supported. The achievement of objective 2 is further detailed 
in section 4.6. The most important decision related disciplines are economics and psychology 
(Harrison, 1999). Rational style is the brainchild of economics (Chater et al., 2003;  Mangalindan, 
2004) whereas intuitive style is the creation of psychology (Luthans, 2000).  So, the different levels 
of agreement on different decision-making styles are due to the fact that Qatars economy is one 
of the richest economies in the world based on GDP per capital, ranking between fifth and seventh 
on world rankings for 2015 and 2016 data compiled by the World Bank, United Nations, and IMF. 
So, decision makers are risk aversion where they tend to prefer certainty to uncertainty, and this 
explains why 27.9% agree and strongly agree on expert heuristic decision-making style, 25.72% 
agree and strongly agree on rational decision-making style, 14.82% agree and strongly agree on 
intuitive decision-making style, 18.8% agree and strongly agree on dependent decision-making 
style, 6.66% agree and strongly agree on spontaneous decision-making style, and 6.1% agree and 
strongly agree on avoidant decision-making style. which means where rational economic 
approaches advocated the economic man who is maximizer in nature and uses all the means to reach 
at an ideal end (Hendry, 2000), intuitive decision-making style is more satisfying in nature (Driver et 
al.,1993) which is more related to feelings, emotions, and impressions (Scott & Bruce, 1995). 
The study investigated the relationship of decision-making styles with executives 
demographics, and it was shown in able 4.14, that H02 (there is NO Statistically Significant 
difference between decision-making styles of executives and their demographics in Qatar) is only 
partially supported. In fact, Factor 1 (Avoidatnt decision-making style) has positive significant 
correlation with number of years in the current business at the 0.05 level, Factor 4 (intuitive 
decision-making style) has positive significant correlation with level of Education at the 0.01 level, 
and F5 (dependent decision-making style) has positive significant correlation with both number of 
years in the current business and level of education at the 0.05 level. Age is not significantly 
correlated with any of the decision-making styles (Objective 3). 
O4: To suggest the direction of improvement, derived from relevant academic research, by 
which executives' decision-making should follow (RQ5). 
P1 Executives in Qatar use a range of decision-making styles, including rational and 
heuristic styles, that can be profiled using a structured questionnaire.

APPENDICES  
APPENDIX 1: QUANTITATIVE RESEARCH QUESTIONNAIRE  
Research Questionnaire Keys 
Items 1-5 DMS Scott and Bruce (1995) 
Rational decision-making style: Rational 
decision-makers conduct an extensive search for 
alternatives and make a logical choice between 
them. 
Items 6-10 DMS Scott and Bruce (1995) 
Intuitive decision-making style: Intuitive 
decision-makers use their intuition to make 
decisions

Dependent decision-making style: Dependent 
decision-makers rely on others to guide their 
decision-making. 
Items 16-20 DMS Scott and Bruce (1995) 
Avoidant decision-making style: Avoidant 
decision-makers avoid making a decision 
whenever possible. 
Item 21-25 DMS Scott and Bruce (1995) 
Spontaneous decision-making style: Spontaneous 
decision-makers have a sense of urgency and 
make rapid decisions.

APPENDIX 2: AGENDA SEMI-STRUCTURED INTERVIEWS  
Agenda for the Semi-Structured Interviews 
Name of the Interviewee: 
Company: 
Position: 
Specialty: 
Years of experience: 
Introduction  
1. What is your position in the company and what is your role?  
2. What is the organizational structure in your company?  
3. How is your company performing?  
4. Do you consider the external environment stable or unstable?  
5. Can you describe what could be a strategic decision for your company?  
6. What type of strategic decisions you are required to make?  
Successful Decision-Making Case  
7. Can you describe a successful strategic decision you made in the past?  
8. Who were the people involved in the decision-making process?  
9. What is the level of importance for the decision made?  
10. What is the level of uncertainty for the decision made?  
11. Would you say that the decision was motivated by an opportunity or by a crisis?  
Rational elements 
12. How thoroughly did the group search and analyse information in making this decision?  
13. Did you use analytic techniques in making the decision? If so, how important were they in 
the process?  
14. How efficient was the group at focusing its attention on crucial information, ignoring 
irrelevant information?  
15. Would you investigate the situation within the company as well as doing a site visit? Then 
would you make a decision on how to proceed based on your findings? 
16. To what extent was the decision affected by the use of authority and influence among group 
members?  
Heuristic elements 
17. Was your professional experience crucial while deliberating for the decision?  
18. Did your personal judgments influence you when making this decision? If so, to what extent?  
19. Did your gut-feeling influence you when making this decision? If so, to what extent? 
20. Are you trying to be as sensitive and as supportive as possible to employees?  
21. Did group members primarily care about their own goals, or with the goals of the 
organization? Did your own personal goals affect the decision?  
Thank you very much for your time. Is there anything you would like to add? 
The following follow up questions can be used during the interview for more clarifications: 
22. Can you explain that further? 
23. Can you give an example of that? 
24. Was there anything unexpected that happened?

APPENDIX 9: LIST OF VARIABLES 
# Variable 
Type of 
Decision 
1 I plan my important decisions carefully. 
Rational 
Decision-making 
Style 
I double-check my information sources to be sure I have the right facts 
before making decisions. 
3 I make decisions in a logical and systematic way. 
4 My decision-making requires careful thought. 
When making a decision, I consider various options in terms of a 
specific goal. 
6 When making decisions, I rely upon my instincts. 
Intuitive 
Decision-making 
Style 
7 When I make decisions, I tend to rely on my intuition. 
8 I generally make decisions which feel right to me. 
It is more important for me to feel that the decision is right than to 
have a rational reason for it 
10 When I make a decision, I trust my inner feelings and reactions 
I often need the assistance of other people when making important 
decisions. 
Dependent 
Decision-making 
Style 
12 When I make important decisions, I am consulting other people 
If I have the support of others, it is easier for me to make important 
decisions 
14 I use the advice of other people in making my important decisions 
I like to have someone to steer me in the right direction when Im 
faced with important decisions. 
16 I avoid making important decisions until the pressure is on. 
Avoidant 
Decision-making 
Style 
17 I postpone decision-making whenever possible. 
18 I often procrastinate when it comes to making important decisions 
19 I generally make important decisions at the last minute. 
I put off making many decisions because thinking about them makes 
me uneasy. 
21 I generally make snap decisions. 
Spontaneous 
Decision-making 
Style 
22 I often make decisions on the spur of the moment. 
23 I make quick decisions. 
24 I often make impulsive decisions. 
25 When making decisions, I do what seems natural at the moment 
# Variable 
Type of 
Decision 
26 I talk to a lot of people when there is a decision to make 
Expert Heuristic 
Decision-making 
Style 
27 I discuss how to make decisions a lot with senior managers 
28 I always consider how decisions made can be applied in wider situations 
I often consider the wider implications of decisions outside the current 
situation 
30 I think about the whole business when making decisions 
31 I often challenge the views of experts when making decisions 
32 I draw on my personal experiences to make decisions 
33 I consider the costs when making decisions 
34 I consider many outcomes and possibilities when making decisions 
35 I look for patterns that I have seen before when making decisions 
36 I use rules of thumb to make decisions 
37 I use some short cuts when making decisions 
I often compare the current situation with similar ones already in my 
memory 
39 I assess characteristics of the current situation to match it with others 
40 Once I have made a decision I may change my original assumptions 
# Variable 
Level of 
Decision 
41 Day to day activities of the business Low 
42 Short term activities 
43 Immediate payment decisions 
44 The allocation of resources 
45 The use of resources 
46 Managers across the organization 
47 Long term activities 
48 How many people to deploy on tasks 
49 Broad organizational issues 
50 Top executives 
51 Strategic decisions High 
# Demographic Variables 
52 Age  
53 Number of Years in the current Business  
54 Highest level of Education 
55 Business Organization/Unit  
APPENDIX 10: SEMI STRUCTURED INTERVIEWS RESPONSES  
SEMI STRUCTURED INTERVIEW-1 
Introduction  
1. What is your position in the company and what is your role?  
My profession is primarily in educational and instructional development, with part-time 
assignment in administration.  
2. What is the organizational structure in your company?  
It is both, functional and divisional structure. 
3. How is your company performing?  
It is performing well and efficiently in light of some semi-restructuring environment.  
4. Do you consider the external environment stable or unstable?  
Very dynamically stable.  
5. Can you describe what could be a strategic decision for your company?  
Restructuring units and outcomes to meet Market and society needs.   
6. What type of strategic decisions you are required to make?  
We are required to provide bottom-up action plans to meet strategic goals.  
Successful Decision Making Case  
7. Can you describe a successful strategic decision you made in the past?  
A successful strategic decision represents the restructuring of units goals and objectives to meet 
international standards, but focus on local needs. 
8. Who were the people involved in the decision-making process?  
The decisions are made at the various divisional levels and are cascaded to units. 
9. What is the level of importance for the decision made?  
Very important. 
10. What is the level of uncertainty for the decision made?  
Moderate uncertainty  
11. Would you say that the decision was motivated by an opportunity or by a crisis?  
The decision was made by opportunity, growth and development. 
Rational elements 
12. How thoroughly did the group search and analyse information in making this decision?  
Very thoroughly and comprehensively  
13. Did you use analytic techniques in making the decision? If so, how important were they 
in the process?  
Yes, and very highly important.  
14. How efficient was the group at focusing its attention on crucial information, ignoring 
irrelevant information?  
Very efficient and effective.  
15. Would you investigate the situation within the company as well as doing a site visit? Then 
would you make a decision on how to proceed based on your findings? 
16. To what extent was the decision affected by the use of authority and influence among 
group members?  
Not very affected.  
Heuristic elements 
17. Was your professional experience crucial while deliberating for the decision?  
Vey crucial.  
18. Did your personal judgments influence you when making this decision? If so, to what 
extent?  
Somewhat. Less than 5%. 
19. Did your gut-feeling influence you when making this decision? If so, to what extent? 
20. Are you trying to be as sensitive and as supportive as possible to employees?  
Yes, but in areas outside performance output.  
21. Did group members primarily care about their own goals, or with the goals of the 
organization? Did your own personal goals affect the decision?  
Primary care was for the organizational needs. My personal goals and needs were seen as part of 
the Organizational needs.  
SEMI STRUCTURED INTERVIEW QUESTIONS-2 
Introduction  
1. What is your position in the company and what is your role?  
My current position title is Director of the Core Curriculum Program (CCP) at Qatar University 
(QU). My roles and responsibilities in brief are:  
 Providing strategic oversight and direction of the Program  
 Acts as a focal point with all stakeholders to ensure maintaining an educational 
environment and progression towards achieving CCP mission, objectives and learning 
outcomes  
2. What is the organizational structure in your company?  
The CCP mostly follows a flat or semi flat organizational structure with no middle management 
now existing between CCP Leadership (CCP Director) and employees (faculty and staff). The 
CCP is employing 21 employees in full-time equivalent (FTE) terms. A number of 11 internal 
committees are involved in the CCP governance structure. These committees provide support to 
the Program leadership in areas of curriculum, strategic planning, assessment, visibility and 
branding, media presence, scheduling, preparing for final exams, student engagement and 
outreach, professional development, updating and revising Program policies and procedures, 
among others. Moreover, a university-wide committee has been formed comprising 
representatives from colleges as well as students from the QU Student Representative Board. This 
committee is also involved in the CCP governance and programmatic oversight.    
3. How is your company performing?  
The achievement of CCP initiatives is regularly evaluated against the set objectives as part of 
strategic planning process. The CCP-established KPIs and initiatives are directly linked to the 
CCPs as well as QUs organizational goals. The CCP is generally performing well and advancing 
towards the achievement of set goals. Specifically, 90% of all actions have been successfully 
implemented, while 10% of them are still in progress for last years initiatives.     
 4. Do you consider the external environment stable or unstable?  
Let me say that the external environment for the CCP can be considered stable. Although the CCP 
has undergone overall enhancement process during the last two years, drastic changes to the 
Program have been avoided. Moreover, the CCP has consolidated collaboration and partnership 
opportunities with key stakeholders, which minimized any potential types of conflict. Although 
blockade on Qatar created some issues with student registration at first, such issues were properly 
managed by QU Leadership. 
5. Can you describe what could be a strategic decision for your company?  
In my viewpoint, a strategic decision is a decision that consequently drives the entire human and 
all other resources toward the achievement of one or more end strategic goals. In my case, the 
Programs vision, mission and objectives guide and harmonize this process. Such a decision is 
taken following an analysis of the Programs status quo, a SWOT analysis for instance. The 
progression towards the achievement of these goals are closely monitored and measured.     
 6. What type of strategic decisions you are required to make?  
At the onset of my ongoing journey with the CCP, most of the strategic decisions I was required 
to make were of analytical nature. I was new to the Program and was required to initiate a very 
complex process to advance the CCP and propose an enhancement plan to address some of the 
Programs shortcomings in a form of a CCP Enhancement Proposal. After two years of experience 
with the Program and with developed relations with stakeholders being built and consolidated, 
most of my decisions took  however controlled  an expertise and intuitive decision-making 
nature. Developing an overall enhancement proposal for our Program was not an easy task; it 
required a very well-structured analytical process yielding into many findings and proposed 
enhancement actions that are now in the process of implementations, hopefully by the beginning 
of Fall 2021 semester.  
Successful Decision Making Case  
7. Can you describe a successful strategic decision you made in the past?  
One of the successful strategic decisions I made was to prepare a CCP enhancement proposal 
involving no drastic changes or imply challenges that might hinder the implementation of 
enhancement actions. By investing quality time studying some previous reports and convening 
meetings with some people in the Program, I recognized many issues with the Program. 
Accordingly, I have met with all the members of my new team and assigned tasks among them. I 
started to contact and convene series of meetings with all stakeholders, including Vice President 
for Academic Affairs, colleges deans, associate deans for academic affairs, heads of departments, 
Program Directors and student representative boards, among others. I had access to a wide volume 
of information. To have all stakeholders involved in the enhancement process, I recommended 
forming a University-wide committee. I have formed an internal Program Review Taskforce to 
prepare the groundwork needed. A SWOT (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats) 
analysis of the current Core Curriculum Program was conducted in light of the QU new strategic 
plan 2018-2022 and QU graduate attributes as well as the benchmarking of our program with top 
universities in the region and the world. The purpose of the SWOT analysis was to examine 
internal and external factors that both positively and negatively affect the program in terms of 
curriculum, assessment, students, faculty, and administrative.

A committee consisting of representatives from all colleges

Extremely important as it would affect the whole university

I would say medium

By both

irrelevant information?

It might be not relevant in our case, but I can say that we scanned the external environment

SEMI STRUCTURED INTERVIEW QUESTIONS-3 
Introduction  
1. What is your position in the company and what is your role?  
Director of Research Planning and Development: 
 Coordinates the implementation and reporting on the research and graduate studies strategy. 
 Responsible for the implementation of core strategic initiatives, such as QU Research 
Priorities, Research Impact Framework, Undergraduate Research, Innovation and Research 
Commercialization. 
 Handles research and graduate studies sector annual reporting and planning. 
 Responsible for the enhancement and support for ethics committees: human subjects, animal 
research, and bio-hazardous material. 
 Oversees the quality assurance procedures in research centers (i.e., ISO). 
 Oversees the development of the research sector policies and procedures. 
 Responsible for the annual performance review of university research centers, the review of 
new research center proposals and the review of change requests from existing centers. 
2. What is the organizational structure in your company?  
http://www.qu.edu.qa/about/organization-structure  
3. How is your company performing?  
Not bad 
 4. Do you consider the external environment stable or unstable?  
External environment is changing rapidly. New universities are being established in Qatar. 
Research funding is changing every year without clear direction. It is a changing environment. 
5. Can you describe what could be a strategic decision for your company?  
We have various decisions on what needs to be done to reach the vision of the university. In 
research sector, we need to decide what areas of research are more important to invest in, for 
example. 
6. What type of strategic decisions you are required to make?  
We make various strategic decisions. Some decisions help us research our vision and achieve the 
university strategy. We have various new initiatives to enhance the university research impact 
(commercialization, national needs). We have also important decision enhancing reputation and 
finding strong partners.    
Successful Decision Making Case  
7. Can you describe a successful strategic decision you made in the past?  
I was responsible for developing the new internal grants systems. We designed new grants to have 
more impact by encouraging faculty to work in groups which include faculty, students, and for 
high impact grant should include the industry. We established KPIs per grant and proposed an 
annual review for the performance of internal grants. This worked and we now have much more 
robust system for internal grants. 
8. Who were the people involved in the decision-making process?  
Stakeholders: representative from colleges and research centers in the university research 
committee 
http://www.qu.edu.qa/about/organization-structure
Related Offices: Research Support office, research planning and development, and college of 
graduate studies 
Higher administration: President and vice president 
9. What is the level of importance for the decision made?  
Extremely important as it affects all research active faculty interested in funding.  
10. What is the level of uncertainty for the decision made?  
Medium as we have benchmarked existing models and looked at success regionally and internally. 
Our main task was to customize it for QU model and ensure it is implemented correctly. 
11. Would you say that the decision was motivated by an opportunity or by a crisis?  
Opportunity. Internal grants were being offered every year without big issues. But the strategic 
direction required a new way of looking at these grants.   
Rational elements 
12. How thoroughly did the group search and analyse information in making this decision?  
I would say we had some bias in looking at different model as some group members had experience 
in certain places. I would say we looked at regional models carefully and did not look deeply 
internationally. 
13. Did you use analytic techniques in making the decision? If so, how important were they 
in the process?  
No analytics except simple statistics were used. Other decision like choosing the research priorities 
we used more sophisticated analytics. 
14. How efficient was the group at focusing its attention on crucial information, ignoring 
irrelevant information?  
We were efficient due to our previous experiences as administrators and researchers. 
15. Would you investigate the situation within the company as well as doing a site visit? Then 
would you make a decision on how to proceed based on your findings? 
Yes, I visited universities in Saudi and Oman to understand their general research governance and 
funding schemes. Also, for research priorities we had various sites visits to our industrial 
stakeholders as well as large events with industry consultation sessions. These experience shape 
the different proposals we develop and then we make decisions. 
16. To what extent was the decision affected by the use of authority and influence among 
group members?  
We have enough time to look at the evidence and collect data. But after some discussion, we need 
to reach a decision so sometimes as a group leader I used my authority to move in certain direction. 
Heuristic elements 
17. Was your professional experience crucial while deliberating for the decision?  
Yes, most committee members had excellent experience and more experienced members had 
larger contribution.  
18. Did your personal judgments influence you when making this decision? If so, to what 
extent?  
Definitely, personal judgements play a role. It is hard to say the extent. Each person has his own 
opinion and background. We tried to look at the same data and make things standard but always 
personal backgrounds of each member is present. 
19. Did your gut-feeling influence you when making this decision? If so, to what extent? 
Not at all. It is a discussion with input from various members. 
20. Are you trying to be as sensitive and as supportive as possible to employees?  
I try to be supportive to the team in providing information and facilitating a platform to share data 
and discuss. I am not sure what sensitive means but we consider each person time and effort to 
ensure tasks can be comfortably. 
21. Did group members primarily care about their own goals, or with the goals of the 
organization? Did your own personal goals affect the decision?  
I think most members care about the organization goal and their unit goal. Personal goals are 
always present as well but working in a group reduces it. 
Thank you very much for you time. Is there anything you would like to add? 
Each project is handled differently depending on the level of impact, the relationship with the 
stakeholders, and expected outcomes. 
The following follow up questions can be used during the interview for more clarifications: 
1) Can you explain that further? 
Some projects are hard to discuss widely with all the stakeholder as you have strong resistance. If 
resistance and access to information is not managed well it can lead to the project failure before 
starting.   
2) Can you give an example of that? 
The new system for faculty and center appraisal. We took high level input from stakeholders. But 
with benchmarking and extensive work, we have developed a complete proposal within a 
committee and presented the final outcome. It was hard to have representatives from these center 
as they was some resistance to change.  
3) Was there anything unexpected that happened? 
No. The systems were refined with stakeholders and we gave them a year to adapt so 
implementation went fine. 
21. Did group members primarily care about their own goals, or with the goals of the 
organization? Did your own personal goals affect the decision?  
I tried to get everyone in my team think beyond their personal goals and focus on the organization 
goal.

APPENDIX 11: COVID-19 IMPACTING ON RESEARCH IN QATAR 
According to the Qatari Ministry of Public Health, the total number of infected people who 
recovered from COVID 19 since the start of the epidemic is 329,853 with 652 deaths (MOPH, 
2021) within a total population of 3,138,210 residents including almost 320.000 Qatari nationals 
and 87% of all residents have had two vaccine doses. The Ministry of Public Health dedicated 
three facilities to accommodate COVID-19 patients: including the Communicable Disease Centre, 
the Cuban Hospital, and Hazm Mebaireek General Hospital. The government allowed partial 
functioning of some workplaces. Yet, a few key workplace settings remained relatively fully 
operational such as the health sector and the airport.  
The Qatari Ministry of Public Health stated Qatar is currently administering the Pfizer/BioNTech 
vaccine and the Moderna vaccine after approving it for emergency use by the Department of 
Pharmacy and Pharmaceutical Control in the Ministry of Public Health noting that it will be free 
of charge for everyone. All citizens and residents aged (12 years and above) could be vaccinated 
regardless of their health conditions although people with a history of severe allergic reaction to 
any component of the vaccine should not take it. During the pre-vaccination assessment carried 
out before each vaccination, the medical team will ask the patient about any allergies and discuss 
this with them. Monitoring everyone receiving the vaccines for a period of up to 15 minutes 
following the vaccination to ensure there are no adverse reactions. The vaccine will be also 
available for recovered people who have been infected although research to date indicates that 
people who have been infected with COVID-19 build-up natural immunity it is unclear how long 
this immunity last for and how effective it is. Pregnant or breastfeeding women have the freedom 
to postpone the vaccine upon doctors request; the third booster dose will be eligible after 6 months 
from the second dose especially for some categories that are in high risk, including: 
 Those receiving cancer treatments to treat tumors or leukemia 
 Those with advanced or untreated HIV infection 
 Those with chronic conditions such as asplenia and chronic kidney disease 
 Those who have had an organ transplant and are using drugs that suppress the immune 
system 
 Those with moderate or severe primary immunodeficiency 
 Those who have had a stem cell transplant within the past two years or are using 
immunosuppressive drugs.  
At the date of writing 931, 418 booster doses have been administered (MOPH, 2022). 
The pandemic decreased the work efficiency due to the restricted lockdown and the way work has 
changed from offices to online from home, even though the researcher had more time to work on 
the research, but still working from the office was preferable so that thoughts could be shared with 
colleagues, keeping in touch with their teams, and collecting data, whereas at home it was better 
to work on the manuscript, reading the literature, and analyse their data. These results draw 
attention to how working from home became a major element of researchers life and those new 
ways of working had to be learnt: along with coping strategies in order to obtain any interviews 
Data collection through interviews was made impossible because of rapidly changing schedules of 
the researcher and any potential interviewee executives. due to the pandemic and the spreading of 
the Covid 19 virus in Qatar. All interviews were initially cancelled due to the quarantine or people 
being afraid to meet and the requirement of social distancing - even the ones that were pushed to 
another date depended on the governmental procedures to deal with the circumstancing and 
interviews were completed with caution. Face to face interviews proved to be very comfortable 
because of the requirement to wear face masks the whole time and social distancing and due to the 
anxiety of participants little deep information was obtained. 
People remain under lockdown and enacted social distancing; making it impossible to have 
relationships as they were before COVID 19. At the most basic level, the way people relate to 
other people outside our households is unlike anything that had ever been experienced. People 
used to engage closely with others in business, recreational, retail and religious settings, but in 
COVID times they now never shake hands and move more rapidly to distance themselves from 
each other. Oral communication proceeds at a distance or preferably via an electronic device. Most 
schools closed and have changed to online teaching and people everywhere, who had always relied 
on teachers and the school infrastructure, now had to use computers and home life became 
increasing difficult. Some parents stopped paying tuition fees for higher education students and 
students become less interested in studying because there is no physical contact with tutors. Parents 
faced difficulties in making their younger children finish any schoolwork and daycare providers 
were closed or were reduced to 20% of their intake. The government decided to stop all incoming 
flights to Doha, from Monday, March 16, 2020 and applied the governmental quarantine laws so 
that home quarantine was mandatory on arrival for all people coming to Qatar from any destination 
and for a period of 14 days. While it is possible to move within the country, public transport 
services, including the Doha metro service and public transport bus services were stopped. Most 
of the industrial area was closed starting on March 17, 2020 and testing for the virus was increased, 
in an attempt to prevent the virus spreading further. However, the government was keen not to 
affect the daily life of the residents of the industrial areas, and the Ministry of Administrative 
Development, Labor and Social Affairs along with the Qatar Charity, provided masks, sterilizers, 
and other protective equipment. Salaries continued to be paid. From March 17, 2020, retail stores 
and bank branches in malls were closed, as were shopping centers (excluding food stores and 
pharmacies), other shops, gyms, salons and club activities in hotels. On March 21, 2020, the Prime 
Minister, the minister of the interior and the chairman of the Supreme Committee for Crisis 
Management issued a decree to impose precautionary measures to prevent all forms of assembly, 
by the authority of the law (such as meeting in parks, public beaches, and all forms of social 
gatherings), in an effort to stop the spread of the Corona virus (Covid-19). The Council of Ministers 
decided (on 18th March, 2020 and strengthen further on 1st April, 2020) to reduce the number of 
employees in government agencies, and workers present at workplaces in the private sector were 
limited to 20% of the total number of employees.  At least 80% of people worked from home.  
Further, The Ministry of Commerce and Industry, in coordination with the relevant authorities, 
also decided to reduce working hours to six working hours per day for essential employees and 
workers who are at their workplace in both the public and private sectors. On April 22, 2020, the 
Council of Ministers decided that employees and workers in the government sectors where most 
workers are in close contact with patients, clients or customers should wear masks to carry out 
their work and tasks, bearing in mind that officials in this sector also provide those masks. On May 
18, 2020, the Council of Ministers decided that all citizens and residents were obligated to install 
and use the EHTERAZ app on smartphones when leaving the house for any reason. EHTERAZ 
tracks the transmission chains of the spread of the Corona virus, providing users with accurate 
information and assisting the medical teams involved in providing health care as and when 
necessary. The app alerts users in the event of a contact with an infected case, ensuring that testing 
and medical care could be administered in a timely manner. Similar measures were undertaken in 
the UK and supervision was restricted to zoom and phone calls rather than face to face. 
Additionally detailed face to face research conversations and discussions over hard copies of 
printed drafts were no longer possible.
